[[proof]]
name = "mathd_numbertheory_765"
iteration = 50
time = 77
proof = """
theorem mathd_numbertheory_765
(x : ℤ)
(h₀ : x < 0)
(h₁ : (24 * x) % 1199 = 15) :
x ≤ -449 := by
  have h_main : x ≤ -449 := by
    by_contra! h
    have h₂ : x ≥ -448 := by linarith
    have h₃ : x ≥ -448 := by linarith
    have h₄ : (24 * x) % 1199 = 15 := h₁
    have h₅ : x ≥ -448 := by linarith
    have h₆ : x ≤ -1 := by
      omega
    -- We will check all possible values of x in the range [-448, -1] to see if any satisfy the condition.
    interval_cases x <;> norm_num [Int.mul_emod, Int.emod_emod] at h₄ <;> omega
  exact h_main
"""
outline = """
### Detailed Proof and Analysis

First, we need to prove that if `x` is an integer less than 0 and `24 * x ≡ 15 mod 1199`, then `x ≤ -449`.

#### Step 1: Understand the Congruence
The congruence `24 * x ≡ 15 mod 1199` means that `1199` divides `24 * x - 15`, i.e., there exists an integer `k` such that:
\\[ 24 * x - 15 = 1199 * k \\]
or equivalently:
\\[ 24 * x = 1199 * k + 15 \\]

Since `x < 0`, we can rearrange the equation to find a lower bound for `x`:
\\[ x = \\frac{1199 * k + 15}{24} \\]

#### Step 2: Find the Range of `k`
We need to find all integers `k` such that `x < 0` and `x` is an integer. 

First, note that `x` is an integer, so `1199 * k + 15` must be divisible by `24`. 

Compute the remainder of `1199 * k + 15` modulo `24`:
\\[ 1199 \\mod 24 = 1199 - 24 \\times 49 = 1199 - 1176 = 23 \\]
Thus:
\\[ 1199 * k + 15 \\equiv 23 * k + 15 \\mod 24 \\]

The condition `24 * x ≡ 15 mod 1199` is equivalent to:
\\[ 23 * k + 15 \\equiv 0 \\mod 24 \\]
because `24 * x ≡ 0 mod 24` and `1199 ≡ 23 mod 24`.

This simplifies to:
\\[ 23 * k \\equiv -15 \\mod 24 \\]
or equivalently:
\\[ 23 * k \\equiv 9 \\mod 24 \\]
because `-15 ≡ 9 mod 24`.

Now, find the multiplicative inverse of `23` modulo `24`. The inverse of `23` modulo `24` is `-1` because:
\\[ 23 * (-1) \\equiv -23 \\equiv 1 \\mod 24 \\]
(since `-23 + 24 = 1`).

Multiply both sides of `23 * k ≡ 9 mod 24` by `-1`:
\\[ k \\equiv -9 \\equiv 15 \\mod 24 \\]

Thus, `k = 24 * m + 15` for some integer `m`.

#### Step 3: Find the Range of `x`
Substitute `k = 24 * m + 15` back into the expression for `x`:
\\[ x = \\frac{1199 * (24 * m + 15) + 15}{24} = \\frac{1199 * 24 * m + 1199 * 15 + 15}{24} = 1199 * m + \\frac{1199 * 15 + 15}{24} \\]
Simplify the numerator:
\\[ 1199 * 15 + 15 = 15 * (1199 + 1) = 15 * 1200 = 18000 \\]
Thus:
\\[ x = 1199 * m + \\frac{18000}{24} = 1199 * m + 750 \\]

But we need to ensure that `x < 0`. Since `m` is a non-negative integer (because `k = 24 * m + 15 ≥ 0` is not possible for `x < 0` as we will see), we can find the smallest `m` such that `x < 0`.

However, we can also consider `m` as a negative integer. 

But we can find a better approach. 

#### Step 4: Find the Smallest `m` Such That `x < 0`
Given `x = 1199 * m + 750`, we need `x < 0`, i.e., `1199 * m + 750 < 0`. 

Since `1199 * m` is negative for `m ≤ -1` and `m ≥ 0`, we can find the smallest `m` such that `1199 * m + 750 < 0`.

For `m = -1`:
\\[ x = 1199 * (-1) + 750 = -1199 + 750 = -449 \\]
For `m ≤ -2`, `x` becomes even smaller. For example, `m = -2`:
\\[ x = 1199 * (-2) + 750 = -2398 + 750 = -1648 < -449 \\]
Thus, the smallest `x` is `-449` when `m = -1`.

But we need to ensure that no `m` gives a larger `x` and `x < 0` is satisfied. 

Alternatively, we can find the smallest `m` such that `1199 * m + 750 < 0`:
\\[ 1199 * m < -750 \\]
\\[ m < \\frac{-750}{1199} \\approx -0.625 \\]
Since `m` is an integer, the smallest `m` is `m = -1`.

Thus, the smallest possible `x` is `-449` when `m = -1`. 

Therefore, `x ≤ -449` is the required bound.

#### Step 5: Verify the Bound
For `m ≥ 0`, `x = 1199 * m + 750 ≥ 750 > 0`, which contradicts `x < 0`. 

For `m ≤ -1`, `x` decreases as `m` decreases. The smallest `x` is `-449` when `m = -1`. 

Thus, `x ≤ -449` is the correct bound.

#### Step 6: Formal Reasoning
1. From `24 * x ≡ 15 mod 1199`, we have `24 * x = 1199 * k + 15` for some integer `k`.
2. Rearrange to `x = (1199 * k + 15) / 24`.
3. Since `x < 0`, `1199 * k + 15 < 0` and `1199 * k + 15` is divisible by `24`.
4. The smallest `k` such that `1199 * k + 15 < 0` is `k = -1`, giving `x = (1199 * (-1) + 15)/24 = (-1199 + 15)/24 = -1184/24 = -296/6 = -148/3`, but this is not an integer. 

   Wait, this is incorrect because `1199 * k + 15` must be divisible by `24` and `1199 * k + 15 < 0`. 

   The correct approach is to find the smallest `k` such that `1199 * k + 15 < 0` and `24` divides `1199 * k + 15`.

   The smallest `k` is `k = -1` because `1199 * (-1) + 15 = -1184` is not divisible by `24` (`-1184 / 24 = -49.333...`). 

   The next smallest `k` is `k = -2`:
   `1199 * (-2) + 15 = -2388 + 15 = -2373` is not divisible by `24` (`-2373 / 24 = -98.875`).

   The next `k` is `k = -3`:
   `1199 * (-3) + 15 = -3597 + 15 = -3582` is not divisible by `24` (`-3582 / 24 = -149.25`).

   The next `k` is `k = -4`:
   `1199 * (-4) + 15 = -4796 + 15 = -4781` is not divisible by `24` (`-4781 / 24 = -199.208...`).

   The next `k` is `k = -5`:
   `1199 * (-5) + 15 = -5995 + 15 = -5980` is not divisible by `24` (`-5980 / 24 = -249.166...`).

   The next `k` is `k = -6`:
   `1199 * (-6) + 15 = -7194 + 15 = -7179` is not divisible by `24` (`-7179 / 24 = -299.125`).

   The next `k` is `k = -7`:
   `1199 * (-7) + 15 = -8393 + 15 = -8378` is not divisible by `24` (`-8378 / 24 = -349.083...`).

   The next `k` is `k = -8`:
   `1199 * (-8) + 15 = -9592 + 15 = -9577` is not divisible by `24` (`-9577 / 24 = -399.041...`).

   The next `k` is `k = -9`:
   `1199 * (-9) + 15 = -10791 + 15 = -10776` is divisible by `24` because `-10776 / 24 = -449`.

   Thus, `k = -9` is the smallest `k` such that `1199 * k + 15 < 0` and `24` divides `1199 * k + 15`.

   Therefore, `x = (1199 * (-9) + 15)/24 = (-10791 + 15)/24 = -10776 / 24 = -449`.

   For `k < -9`, `x` becomes smaller, e.g., `k = -10`:
   `x = (1199 * (-10) + 15)/24 = (-11990 + 15)/24 = -11975 / 24 = -498.958... < -449`.

   Hence, the smallest `x` is `-449` when `k = -9`.

   Therefore, `x ≤ -449` is the correct bound.

#### Step 7: Conclusion
The smallest possible `x` is `-449`, and for all other `k`, `x` is smaller. Hence, `x ≤ -449` is the required bound.

### Step-by-Step Abstract Plan

1. **Understand the Congruence**:
   - The condition `24 * x ≡ 15 mod 1199` is equivalent to `1199` divides `24 * x - 15`, i.e., `24 * x = 1199 * k + 15` for some integer `k`.

2. **Find the Range of `k`**:
   - Since `x < 0`, `1199 * k + 15 < 0` and `24` divides `1199 * k + 15`.
   - Find the smallest `k` such that `1199 * k + 15 < 0` and `24` divides `1199 * k + 15`.

3. **Find the Smallest `k`**:
   - Test small negative `k` to find the smallest `k` satisfying the conditions.
   - The smallest `k` is `k = -9`, giving `x = -449`.

4. **Verify the Bound**:
   - For `k < -9`, `x` becomes smaller, e.g., `x = -498.958... < -449`.
   - Thus, `x ≤ -449` is the correct bound.
